(K.) The doing this is repeatedly forbidden in traditions: but what is meant thereby is, one's doing so in the belief that he may attain by it something which God has not decreed to betide him, or that he may divert from himself something decreed to befall him: yet if he do so, fulfilment is obligatory on him. (IAth.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">نَذَرَ الوَلَدَ</foreign>, (M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">نَذَرَتْهُ</foreign>, (M,) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> (the father, M, K) and <hi rend="ital">she</hi> (the mother, M) <hi rend="ital">appointed the child</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by a vow</hi>] <hi rend="ital">to be a minister</hi> or <hi rend="ital">servant to the church,</hi> (M, K,) or <hi rend="ital">to a place appropriated to religious services</hi> or <hi rend="ital">exercises,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">acts of devotion:</hi> (TA:) so in the Kur, iii. 31. (M.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">نَذِرَ بِالشَّىْءِ</foreign>, aor.

                  <hi rend="ital">The people warned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">cautioned, one another,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">put one another in fear,</hi> (M, K,) of a terrifying evil. (TA.) You say <foreign lang="ar">تناذر القَوْمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The people warned one another,</hi> (S,) <hi rend="ital">and put one another in fear, of such a thing.</hi> (S, A.)
